<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2210446009514775087"><strong>The true story, originally published as <em>Rocket Boys</em>, that inspired the Universal Pictures film.<br /></strong><br />It was 1957, the year Sputnik raced across the Appalachian sky, and the small town of Coalwood, West Virginia, was slowly dying. <br /><br />Faced with an uncertain future, Homer Hickam nurtured a dream: to send rockets into outer space. The introspective son of the mine’s superintendent and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2210446009514775087"><strong>The true story, originally published as <em>Rocket Boys</em>, that inspired the Universal Pictures film.<br /></strong><br />It was 1957, the year Sputnik raced across the Appalachian sky, and the small town of Coalwood, West Virginia, was slowly dying. <br /><br />Faced with an uncertain future, Homer Hickam nurtured a dream: to send rockets into outer space. The introspective son of the mine’s superintendent and a mother determined to get him out of Coalwood forever, Homer fell in with a group of misfits who learned not only how to turn scraps of metal into sophisticated rockets but how to sustain their hope in a town that swallowed its men alive.<br /><br />As the boys began to light up the tarry skies with their flaming projectiles and dreams of glory, Coalwood, and the Hickams, would never be the same.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_22010580">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22010580" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/257424-erin" class="left imgcol" title="Erin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1186779984p2/257424.jpg" alt="Erin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/22010580?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 11, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/257424-erin" class="user" title="Erin">Erin</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96642.Rocket_Boys" title="Paperback 9780385333214" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22010580">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3504419229044138841">If there is one, just ONE thing that was monumentally historic in this book, a revealing glimpse into our culture's rich history and sociological mindset, it had nothing to do with rockets.<br /><br />DID ANYONE ELSE NOTICE, THAT FIFTY YEARS AGO, PEOPLE WERE HOOKING UP IN BAND BUSES!?<br /><br />Holy mother of french horns, it's ingrained in our history. I'm not talking to you, ex-cheerleaders belonging to the "'Twilight' fanclubs", you emo english lit majors arguing over poe. You couldn't understand. <br /><br />Only a certain ty</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3504419229044138841">If there is one, just ONE thing that was monumentally historic in this book, a revealing glimpse into our culture's rich history and sociological mindset, it had nothing to do with rockets.<br /><br />DID ANYONE ELSE NOTICE, THAT FIFTY YEARS AGO, PEOPLE WERE HOOKING UP IN BAND BUSES!?<br /><br />Holy mother of french horns, it's ingrained in our history. I'm not talking to you, ex-cheerleaders belonging to the "'Twilight' fanclubs", you emo english lit majors arguing over poe. You couldn't understand. <br /><br />Only a certain type of person--- a special combination of musicianship, athleticism and geekiness, if you will--- will truly comprehend the depth of connection I felt after reading Homer's elation at having Dorothy Plunk drift off to sleep on his shoulder while the bus plowed through West Virginia backcountry. That beautiful contentedness with the world, that feeling of satisfaction at the day's performance, the wind whipping through your hair, cuddled up for warmth with half the trumpet section as your dirty, poorly maintained and diesel belching bus careens through the night at the hands of some ill-trained and half asleep band booster.<br /><br />*sigh*<br /><br />I mean, serious relationships all over this country have been SOLD on late night band bus trips. Marriages made. Babies born (after the marriages, i mean. we're not cheerleaders, afterall). I'm willing to bet that thousand of American teenagers would never have logged thousands of solid make-out practice hours without this type of magical transportation.I just never guessed it had been around for so long. It's like discovering your great ancestors also signed in at the gym just to get a smoothie so their account would show they came more than three times a week and were actually using their membership. anyway, i digress.<br /><br />solid book. can't beat the style of writing, it may be slow, but it matches his personality so completely you know it must be genuine. and somehow, for it, the pay off in the end is greater--- i was heartbroken to read the epilogue about dorothy, that she was even the first part of it at all.<br /><br /><br />homer, i really liked you, man. you should have known, the woodwinds can be a bitch. because i feel like we're friends, and it's never too late for a rocket scientist (you charmer!) ... you can NEVER go wrong with a percussionist.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3504419229044138841">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_152592282">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152592282" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3891953-cass" class="left imgcol" title="Cass"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295560151p2/3891953.jpg" alt="Cass" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/152592282?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 19, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3891953-cass" class="user" title="Cass">Cass</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96642.Rocket_Boys" title="Paperback 9780385333214" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=2011" class="actionLinkLite">2011</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=biography" class="actionLinkLite">biography</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=true-stories" class="actionLinkLite">true-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152592282">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17696623132946543468">This book was fabulous. It is the type of book I will be lending to everyone. It is mostly a true story (though the author admits to taking some license) about Homer Hickam, Jr. and his rocket building club. Hickam grew up in a mining town in which the only job choice was to become a miner. His mother wanted to ensure he got out of the town and encouraged him to build rockets as a means of proving to his father that he was smart enough to go to college.<br /><br />This book inspired the movie <em>October Sky</em> wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17696623132946543468">This book was fabulous. It is the type of book I will be lending to everyone. It is mostly a true story (though the author admits to taking some license) about Homer Hickam, Jr. and his rocket building club. Hickam grew up in a mining town in which the only job choice was to become a miner. His mother wanted to ensure he got out of the town and encouraged him to build rockets as a means of proving to his father that he was smart enough to go to college.<br /><br />This book inspired the movie <em>October Sky</em> which has long been a favourite feel good movie of mine. However I think I like the book for an entirely different reason. The movie is an inspirational story of a boy overcoming the odds in order to become something that was not expected of him. While the book was about that too, it was also about a lifestyle in which children where given much greater freedoms and responsibilities.<br /><br />When Hickam and his buddies decided to build a rocket they went to the corner store and bought explosive chemicals in order to make it happen. When they blew up his mother's fence her reaction was to encourage him to build more and to not blow himself up. The rocket launches were incredible dangerous especially to spectators who were repeatedly diving for cars in order to avoid being impaled by rockets. Twice he describes rockets that went out of control and ended up in the town itself, potentially deadly weapons.<br /><br />The story that stands out in my mind is of Hickam and his mates riding there sleds many miles to school after a snow day was declared. He ended up getting home on his own, walking through a whiteout and suffering near frostbite before coming across a home in which he was invited. He dried off and then kept on going. On arriving home his mother and father were unperplexed, not slightly bothered that there son could almost have died.<br /><br />I wonder whether the Hickam's mother was so passionate about him leaving the town that she thought it better that he die trying than have to go down into the mines.<br /><br />I found this book inspirational as a parent. It reminded me that children become adults quicker than we think, and are capable of much more than our current system allows for.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17696623132946543468">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1780834-mark-mallett" class="user" title="Mark Mallett">Mark Mallett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96642.Rocket_Boys" title="Paperback 9780385333214" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1780834-mark-mallett?shelf=nonfiction" class="actionLinkLite">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1780834-mark-mallett?shelf=memoir" class="actionLinkLite">memoir</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39731582">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5283828462680859807">Interesting that "October Sky" (the name of the movie) is an anagram of "Rocket Boys" (the name of the book - the original name anyway).<br /><br />Although I was a teenager more than a decade later than Hickam was, some of the things he wrote about hit close to home. I, too, grew up in a rural area - on a dirt road in the woods of NH. I remember what it's like to lie in the dark in the middle of nowhere and watch for satellites. I and my circle of friends experimented pretty freely on our own with things l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5283828462680859807">Interesting that "October Sky" (the name of the movie) is an anagram of "Rocket Boys" (the name of the book - the original name anyway).<br /><br />Although I was a teenager more than a decade later than Hickam was, some of the things he wrote about hit close to home. I, too, grew up in a rural area - on a dirt road in the woods of NH. I remember what it's like to lie in the dark in the middle of nowhere and watch for satellites. I and my circle of friends experimented pretty freely on our own with things like chemistry and electricity, and did things like making powder-propelled projectiles. We did not achieve Hickam's level or come anywhere near his scientific approach, but nevertheless remembering these things made me feel a connection to his tale. Whether that's important, I can't say, but I doubt it. I think everyone can empathize with a quest for intellectual independence.<br /><br />One thing that struck me was how well Hickam constructed, or perhaps experienced, parallels to what the boys are doing with their rockets. This is a story of bonds that can be loosened but only to varying degrees. It's told in terms of the rockets that fight against gravity, only to return; of young people stretching their roots, only to retain them; of a mining town that has to give up its hold on its people (or vice versa). Very telling is Hickam finding a favorite poem of his father, about sending out dreams in cars that come back empty.<br /><br />Way too long a note, I know..<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5283828462680859807">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1096904313">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1096904313?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20048096-pamela" class="user" title="Pamela">Pamela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=biography-memoir" class="actionLinkLite">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=coming-of-age" class="actionLinkLite">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=family" class="actionLinkLite">family</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=southern-non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">southern-non-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=cold-war" class="actionLinkLite">cold-war</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=friendship" class="actionLinkLite">friendship</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=science" class="actionLinkLite">science</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=aviation" class="actionLinkLite">aviation</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=west-virginia" class="actionLinkLite">west-virginia</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=book-to-film" class="actionLinkLite">book-to-film</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=space" class="actionLinkLite">space</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1096904313">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4870105450891324619">During the eighties I was the store manager for Toys and Gifts Outlet in Oklahoma City. Loved that job! It was comprised of many elements I enjoy: creativity, organization, team-building, spatial aptitude, business mathematics, diversity, physicality and social interaction. Being a decade before the microchip exploded onto the scene in full force – kids, and adults alike, still found joy in non-computerized toys and hobbies that required a bit of mentality, physicality, skill, and/or self-genera</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4870105450891324619">During the eighties I was the store manager for Toys and Gifts Outlet in Oklahoma City. Loved that job! It was comprised of many elements I enjoy: creativity, organization, team-building, spatial aptitude, business mathematics, diversity, physicality and social interaction. Being a decade before the microchip exploded onto the scene in full force – kids, and adults alike, still found joy in non-computerized toys and hobbies that required a bit of mentality, physicality, skill, and/or self-generated imagination: Frisbees, board games, kites, yoyos, roller skates, Rubik Cubes, croquet, Spiro-Graphs, weaving looms, art kits, science kits, model cars, model planes, telescopes and the highly sought after – Estes Model Rocket kits and engines. <br /><br />In which I never understood the thrill of rocketry until my assistant manager, Richard Wood, held a rocket building clinic one Saturday morning in the field behind our mall. At clinics end, they lit-off one of Rick’s personal rockets. And wow! Just like the town folk of Coalwood, West Virginia, in Hickman’s memoir – October Sky (Rocket Boys) - that gathered to watch, I was mouth-open, dumbstruck-awed! Though Rick’s twenty-two inch, twenty-five-thousand ft flight Hercules rocket hardly compared to the steel prototypes invented, designed, built, tooled, fueled, and flown by Hickman and the other “Rocket Boys,” it was still way cool impressive. <br /><br />Equally so, I was impressed with Hickman’s memoir – a time capsule of sorts that encompasses: rocketry, the race to space; cold-war-era fears and feats; coal mining; family dynamics; friendship; teenage wows and woes coming-of-age in the nineteen-fifties. It was like stepping back in time to witness a by-gone era on the verge of great scientific and technological advancements but with the added bonus of an intimate stroll down Memory Lane. And for the most part, I found that Hickman’s inclusion of intimate details surrounding his personal life, music, school, friendships, parent-son complexities, love quests, cars, and social endeavors gave warmth, humor, era insight, and humanistic value to his memoir. However, a strength carried to excess becomes a weakness. There were a few places that bogged-down with frivolous microscopic details; black holes (rabbit trails) of no significance that made the book lengthier than need be, in my opinion. <br /><br />Overall, taking in account black holes, “October Sky is a four-star-propulsion great read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4870105450891324619">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_335133896">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/335133896" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8297884-m-j-johnson" class="left imgcol" title="M.J. Johnson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1338547819p2/8297884.jpg" alt="M.J. Johnson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/335133896?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8297884-m-j-johnson" class="user" title="M.J. Johnson">M.J. Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13597019-october-sky" title=" " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8297884-m-j-johnson?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer335133896">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1937880627986400217">When in Wales recently I finished reading October Sky by Homer H Hickam, which seemed to have a certain synchronicity for me at that moment in time. The book is set in Coalwood, West Virginia, a long way from Aberdare in the valleys of South Wales where I spent my earliest years and where its unmissable cemetery is the final resting place for generations of my ancestors. Mining was the lifeblood of both Coalwood and Aberdare, and my grandfather died from the same miners' lung disease that took H</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1937880627986400217">When in Wales recently I finished reading October Sky by Homer H Hickam, which seemed to have a certain synchronicity for me at that moment in time. The book is set in Coalwood, West Virginia, a long way from Aberdare in the valleys of South Wales where I spent my earliest years and where its unmissable cemetery is the final resting place for generations of my ancestors. Mining was the lifeblood of both Coalwood and Aberdare, and my grandfather died from the same miners' lung disease that took Homer Hickam's father. However, October Sky is also about the young Homer's fascination with rockets and his boyish indignation at the Russians who are at that time (Sputnik, 1957) winning the Space Race. He and a bunch of friends decide to set the record straight and gradually their endeavours are taken up and proudly supported by the folk of Coalwood. It is everything its reviewers claim with all the clichéd words you'd expect to find on any cover for any rites of passage tale, "Absorbing ... wonderful ... funny ... painful ... inspirational," however, for this book every one of these words is applicable and accurate.<br /><br />It is a joy to read and it's not difficult to understand why it's been compared to To Kill a Mockingbird. This book has a similar sense of mood and wonderment about it as that fine American twentieth-century classic does (and yes, I still feel bitter that anyone could give T K a M one star on Amazon! Grrr!). The book October Sky was originally published in 1998 as Rocket Boys and I believe it was also made into a movie, however, not one that I've ever seen or recall hearing about.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1937880627986400217">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer179376320">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6029585659102872800">Homer Hickam recounts how he and his classmates, inspired by the launch of Sputnick, taught themselves (with a little help from some key adults) how to build rockets in the late 1950s. Hickam proves himself a more than capable storyteller, mixing equal parts nostalgia, humor, and teenage angst as he tells his story, including a warts-and-all look at his hometown and the coal company which gave it life. The result is a finely crafted tale of heartbreak and consternation, despair and, ultimately,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6029585659102872800">Homer Hickam recounts how he and his classmates, inspired by the launch of Sputnick, taught themselves (with a little help from some key adults) how to build rockets in the late 1950s. Hickam proves himself a more than capable storyteller, mixing equal parts nostalgia, humor, and teenage angst as he tells his story, including a warts-and-all look at his hometown and the coal company which gave it life. The result is a finely crafted tale of heartbreak and consternation, despair and, ultimately, triumph.<br /><br />His relationship with his parents was compelling in its complexity, and I appreciated the honest look at himself, his strengths and foibles, as he progressed through his journey.<br /><br />A first rate book.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/315818-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/315818-kim?shelf=nonfictionmemoir" class="actionLinkLite">nonfictionmemoir</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5239186">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17609412959399173463">I just finished reading this wonderful memoir of six boys growing up in a dead-end coal-mining town in West Virginia. The writing is lyrical and wholesome, yet quietly incisive, similar to Harper Lee's To Kill a Mockingbird. Hickam interweaves several stories with incredible skill, evoking the dreams and sorrows of teenage boys, recalling the nascent years of the space race, describing the hardships of living in southern West Virginia when coal was king. I highly recommend it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9191814-frances-scott?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9191814-frances-scott?shelf=union-township" class="actionLinkLite">union-township</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer350247557">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4083674666871665970">This is one of the books that reminds me why I love being in a book club - it forces me to read books I would never have selected to read or even become aware of.<br /><br />I was fairly certain I would not like this book, and I read the first chapter with a negative predisposition toward it, just to decide whether I would actually read it. About ten chapters later, I realized I could not have been more wrong. I was absolutely hooked and I never looked back.<br /><br />It's one of the best, most inspiring stories I've</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4083674666871665970">This is one of the books that reminds me why I love being in a book club - it forces me to read books I would never have selected to read or even become aware of.<br /><br />I was fairly certain I would not like this book, and I read the first chapter with a negative predisposition toward it, just to decide whether I would actually read it. About ten chapters later, I realized I could not have been more wrong. I was absolutely hooked and I never looked back.<br /><br />It's one of the best, most inspiring stories I've ever read. It is close to perfection as a memoir; writing so good that you don't even notice it; a great story; a lot of depth of interpersonal relationships; extremely appealing characters; a difficult father-son relationship with a believable and satisfying resolution; a teacher who believes in her students and stands by them at all costs. A story of tenacity, of teamwork, of rising above circumstances and background, of refusing to accept the limits imposed by one's environment of origin. Simply put, a wonderful story almost too good for words. It defies description. It is a MUST-READ!<br /><br />PS - The movie based on the book is called October Sky. It's not bad, but it misses a lot of the undercurrents that make the book so great. See the movie but only if you promise not to "pass" on the book!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4083674666871665970">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/30211918-holly-ahaus" class="user" title="Holly Ahaus">Holly Ahaus</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13597019-october-sky" title=" " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/30211918-holly-ahaus?shelf=2014-summer-reading" class="actionLinkLite">2014-summer-reading</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/30211918-holly-ahaus?shelf=gcisd-s-25-book-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">gcisd-s-25-book-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1041967730">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5806498356486697819">I personally enjoy reading memoirs because it's not an autobiography that's like "hey here's some general stuff about me" but rather a personal interpretation of the most important time of a person's life. And who's to know if it's hyperbole, opinion, or straight fact? No one, but it's always told the way it should be. That's the vibe I got from October Sky. I can imagine Homer Hickam sitting somewhere trying to come up with the best way to describe the dread he felt towards working in the mine,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5806498356486697819">I personally enjoy reading memoirs because it's not an autobiography that's like "hey here's some general stuff about me" but rather a personal interpretation of the most important time of a person's life. And who's to know if it's hyperbole, opinion, or straight fact? No one, but it's always told the way it should be. That's the vibe I got from October Sky. I can imagine Homer Hickam sitting somewhere trying to come up with the best way to describe the dread he felt towards working in the mine, the resentment he held toward his brother, the reverence he had for Miss Riley, and the intense effort that went into creating the rocket(s). He should be very proud of the final copy he created, and I must say, I'm fascinated by the story he retold. This is the true American tale of passion, intelligence, and just a bit of rebellion that makes for the ultimate (true) story. I highly recommend it to all lovers of science, memoirs, and feel good endings.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/42771851-derek-wentling" class="left imgcol" title="Derek Wentling"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Derek Wentling" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1286756234?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/42771851-derek-wentling" class="user" title="Derek Wentling">Derek Wentling</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/42771851-derek-wentling?shelf=october-sky" class="actionLinkLite">october-sky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1286756234">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1290722486852574511">The narrator of the book is Homer Hickam Jr, and this was a first person narration story. The narrator is a reliable source due to the fact that this is his actual life story that he is telling. The time period of this book is in the late 1950’s and is set in Coalwood West Virginia. The author of the book is Homer Hickam. He tells his life story of growing up and having a dream to build and work on rockets. Homer Hickam had first published this book as Rocket Boys and it later was renamed to Oct</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1290722486852574511">The narrator of the book is Homer Hickam Jr, and this was a first person narration story. The narrator is a reliable source due to the fact that this is his actual life story that he is telling. The time period of this book is in the late 1950’s and is set in Coalwood West Virginia. The author of the book is Homer Hickam. He tells his life story of growing up and having a dream to build and work on rockets. Homer Hickam had first published this book as Rocket Boys and it later was renamed to October Sky. The setting of this book helped influence the book by showing the difficulties and conflicts that affected Homer Hickam Jr and his dream to build rockets. The overall theme of this book as I saw it was if you can dream it then you can achieve it. This book really shows how you can chase your dreams and with some hard work and determination you can accomplish them. The genre of this book is a nonfiction and a memoir. I don’t think this book compares to any other book out there. It is a one of a kind and can’t really be compared to another book due to the fact that it is a story about someone’s life and no two people live the same exact life or lifestyle even. The plot of the book is all about the space race and how the United States was falling behind. I really enjoyed reading this book. I enjoyed it so much because it showed that dreams can come true and that no matter how difficult it is or how many people tell you that you can’t do it, if you keep trying you will eventually achieve it. Even though I enjoyed this book so much I don’t think I would read another book by this author because I feel I would be disappointed if the next book didn’t live up to this book’s standards. I do however encourage everyone to read this book. It has great lessons on how to live life to the fullest and how to achieve your goals set in life. This is one of the best books I have ever read and I was very inspired by the book. I give this book a rating of 4 out of 5.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1290722486852574511">...more</a>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1177512093" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8332956-just-a-bean" class="left imgcol" title="Just A. Bean"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1332442552p2/8332956.jpg" alt="Just A. Bean" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1177512093?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8332956-just-a-bean" class="user" title="Just A. Bean">Just A. Bean</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1081842.Rocket_Boys" title="Hardcover 9780613366359" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8332956-just-a-bean?shelf=non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8332956-just-a-bean?shelf=history" class="actionLinkLite">history</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8332956-just-a-bean?shelf=aviation-space" class="actionLinkLite">aviation-space</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8332956-just-a-bean?shelf=american" class="actionLinkLite">american</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1177512093">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7584018906647532149">Very similar to the film, for those who have seen it, though lacking the extra drama in the second act. Unsurprisingly, the book pulls most of its tension from Sonny's emotional state, not from external threats, which, when they pop up, are dealt with almost immediately. It worked in the book, and the prose is smooth and humorous. The author mentioned changing things around a bit for narrative flow, but it made a good enough story that it's difficult to mind.<br /><br />All of the rocket building and explos</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7584018906647532149">Very similar to the film, for those who have seen it, though lacking the extra drama in the second act. Unsurprisingly, the book pulls most of its tension from Sonny's emotional state, not from external threats, which, when they pop up, are dealt with almost immediately. It worked in the book, and the prose is smooth and humorous. The author mentioned changing things around a bit for narrative flow, but it made a good enough story that it's difficult to mind.<br /><br />All of the rocket building and explosions were fun, and I appreciated how clearly explained all the science was, but the core of the story is Sonny's family and life in a coal mining town just as coal is going bust. I loved the portrayal of Sonny's complicated relationship with his father, and the strength of his connection with is mother. I know there's a million coming of age stories featuring boys and difficult fathers, but the balance of being a competent and even heroic man and still kind of failing at human interaction really grabbed me here. I also liked that the labour politics were more nuanced than in the film.<br /><br />It's very much a boys own adventure story, and while women aren't completely excluded or unimportant, you get a pretty strong idea that they were not going to get to build rockets any time soon. Nor were the black people down the way, given how heavily Sonny relied on his father's patronage and the town's support. Additionally, one has to wonder if the conversation regarding the ethics of hero-worshipping an ex-Nazi actually happened, or was added after the worst about Wernher von Braun came to light.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7584018906647532149">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1271550614">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1271550614" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/42768556-shelby-kin" class="left imgcol" title="Shelby Kin"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Shelby Kin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1271550614?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/42768556-shelby-kin" class="user" title="Shelby Kin">Shelby Kin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1271550614">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12572947693194126100">The American Classic, October Sky, was written and narrated by the well-known author, Homer Hickam Jr. His memoir was based off the life in Coalwood, West Virginia around the time of the launching of Sputnik, October 1957. This novel was written in first-person, describing Homer's childhood events that started his rocket career. The mining setting allowed "Sonny" to get the right materials and the space he needed to build his rockets. As Sonny's only way out of the mining business and Coalwood,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12572947693194126100">The American Classic, October Sky, was written and narrated by the well-known author, Homer Hickam Jr. His memoir was based off the life in Coalwood, West Virginia around the time of the launching of Sputnik, October 1957. This novel was written in first-person, describing Homer's childhood events that started his rocket career. The mining setting allowed "Sonny" to get the right materials and the space he needed to build his rockets. As Sonny's only way out of the mining business and Coalwood, he looked up to Werner von Braun and had a dream to one day be in Cape Canaveral. I would rate this memoir a 5/5, because it will keep its importance as time goes on and will continue to show people that you can do anything you want in life. Throughout the novel, Sonny proved that with a determined mind set and hard work, you can take yourself where ever you dream. I liked this book a lot because the characters all over came difficult times in their lives, like Sonny believing in himself to accomplish what he wanted to and his father coping with his health issues. I would definitely read more books written by Homer Hickam Jr. because he made me interested in the book using descriptive language, allowing the reader to feel like they were living his childhood in the book. I recommend others to read October Sky, so that everyone can find out that you can achieve your dreams. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12572947693194126100">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13832267080274063822">THIS BOOK WAS SO GOOD AND I WILL ALWAYS HOLD IT CLOSE TO ME. A uniquely American memoir, Rocket Boys tells the story of Homer and his friends' endeavors into the art of rocket building. It was funny and believable and smart and undeniably interesting. A couple of miners' sons from West Virginia did something so great and so important, and that in itself is enough to make the book a classic (in my opinion). I am in awe of all that was accomplished and so eloquently stated in this incredible memoi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13832267080274063822">THIS BOOK WAS SO GOOD AND I WILL ALWAYS HOLD IT CLOSE TO ME. A uniquely American memoir, Rocket Boys tells the story of Homer and his friends' endeavors into the art of rocket building. It was funny and believable and smart and undeniably interesting. A couple of miners' sons from West Virginia did something so great and so important, and that in itself is enough to make the book a classic (in my opinion). I am in awe of all that was accomplished and so eloquently stated in this incredible memoir. I loved it all. I loved hearing about Homer's love for Dorothy Plunk. I loved watching him look into the craggy mountains with Daisy Mae by his side. I loved taking home the science fair medals and rejoicing with all of Coalwood. Above all (pun intended), I loved seeing the rockets launch steadily into the sky, rising higher and higher in a cloud of symbolism and glory. Fans of Billy Bryson's The Life &amp; Times of Thunderbolt Kid will love this book. Rocket Boys epitomizes the reason I read--to learn the life of someone else and a bit more knowledge about the world. To understand more about what it is to be human...to have hopes and loves and sorrows, beginnings and endings. Reading makes me a better person. In fact, it's been shown to make people more empathetic, so I'm not exaggerating. Rocket Boys made me a better person because I am so honored to live in a place where anything is possible, cheesy as it is. There is hope for us all, I hope.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/304659.Rocket_Boys" title="Hardcover 9780385333207" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4828849-michael-burnam-fink?shelf=history" class="actionLinkLite">history</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4828849-michael-burnam-fink?shelf=biography" class="actionLinkLite">biography</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer451501069">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6341842144176450031">There are moments that feel like they'll last forever, moments that tie the smallest lives to the grandest events. One of those moments was Sputnik in 1957, when a boy in West Virginia looked at a moving light in the sky, and dreamed that he would build a rocket. But unlike a thousand other dreamers, Homer Hickham built his rockets, and in 'Rocket Boys' he takes us back to his childhood in Coalwood, and way in which a whole town achieved escape velocity from the daily tyranny of mining and high</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6341842144176450031">There are moments that feel like they'll last forever, moments that tie the smallest lives to the grandest events. One of those moments was Sputnik in 1957, when a boy in West Virginia looked at a moving light in the sky, and dreamed that he would build a rocket. But unlike a thousand other dreamers, Homer Hickham built his rockets, and in 'Rocket Boys' he takes us back to his childhood in Coalwood, and way in which a whole town achieved escape velocity from the daily tyranny of mining and high school football to dream of the skies.<br /><br />This book is triumphant, melancholic, nostalgic, and deeply true. Every awkward dreamer and uncertain utopian will see themselves reflected in Homer Hickham. Right now, his childhood seems more real than my own. The story effortlessly blends the personal tribulations of family and high school, scrounging and bartering materials for rockets, and scientific progress from amateur bomb maker to the second best rocket scientist in the United States (#1 being Werner Von Braun).<br /><br />The only thing that disappoints me with this book is that today, it is much harder to follow in Hickham's footsteps. As a national, we are less adventurous, less crafty, less willing to risk explosions and fire in pursuit of our dreams. But we still have Rocket Boys,</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8429056633796557282">Personally I though October Sky was a great book. The book goes through all of the emotions. Some of the emotions included were sympathy, happiness, and eagerness to get to next page. I’ll have to say. I almost put the book down in the beginning. The ending was kind of a little sadder than I thought it wo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8429056633796557282">Personally I though October Sky was a great book. The book goes through all of the emotions. Some of the emotions included were sympathy, happiness, and eagerness to get to next page. I’ll have to say. I almost put the book down in the beginning. After you get through the fifty pages or introduction, the book gets real good. I was actually surprised how good it got to be when I got to the “juicy” part of the book. It had a great ending. The ending was kind of a little sadder than I thought it would.<br /><br />Now let me tell you my favorites and most hated events or people in this book. My favorite character in this book was Sonny because he knew what he wanted and reached for it. That is what I like. I like when people know what the want and try to get it with all of their strength. My most hated character in the book was Sonny’s dad. He cared more about that mine than his own family. He also didn’t treat his son as equally important. He gave Jim more an interest than Sonny because Jim was on the important “football team.” My favorite part of the book is when Sonny’s dad finnaly started to pay attention to him. My least favorite part of the book is when his cat, Daisy Mae, got killed by one of the mad miners. It was kind of depressing when he was burying the cat and crying all over the place.<br /></span>

      <a href="/user/show/6925718-paul" class="user" title="Paul">Paul</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer233555575">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1777672496021503355">Rocket Boys is a heart-felt story written by Homer H.Hickham,Jr. that shows the true ambition and strength of boy who completes his Journey by putting his mind to it. Homer H.Hickham, better known as Sonny in the book, is a teenager who lives in Coalwood, Virgina. Sonny,as they call him has always been very intellegant from the start. He would always do more than what was asked of him and it is one of the reasons why he made it to where he wanted to go. Growing up Sonny lived with his parents Ho</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1777672496021503355">Rocket Boys is a heart-felt story written by Homer H.Hickham,Jr. that shows the true ambition and strength of boy who completes his Journey by putting his mind to it. Homer H.Hickham, better known as Sonny in the book, is a teenager who lives in Coalwood, Virgina. Sonny,as they call him has always been very intellegant from the start. He would always do more than what was asked of him and it is one of the reasons why he made it to where he wanted to go. Growing up Sonny lived with his parents Homer Sr. and Elise, and his older brother Jim. Sonny and his father have a very strange and usual relationship, you could call it being loved "Unconditionally". His father looks at Sonny has basically nothing, and his older brother Jim is the " Golden Child". Jim is a star football player and everyone loves him, in his fathers eyes he does no wrong. Elise, Sonny's mother is the only person that truly belives in Sonny, she thinks he will grow up and do something great, and not have to work in the dusty old Coalmind like everyone before him. Sonny has 4 best friends that he has know forever, Quentin, Jimmy,Roy Lee , and Sherman. These 5 boys become so interested and amazed by Rockets that they create a group call Rocket Boys. They go through many trials of flying these Rockets ,but they just cant seem to get it to go high enough. As the story goes on Homer Sr. devlopes lung Cancer in his throat from working in the mine so long, it doesn't phase him a bit and he still goes back to work. Sonny's mother then decides to move to myrtle beach, the place she has always wanted to live. She tell him he can come with her or stay and die in the factory, he choses the factory. On Sonny's final day of highschool, the boys met as usual to test there rocket, this time they have a large crowd watching them as they are about to do liftoff. As they pressed the button and the rocket goes soaring in the air, it reaches the highest it as ever reached before. Among the crowd was his father, he came up to Sonny and told him how proud he was of him , Sonny finally felt like his father accepted him. Rocket Boys is a very inspiring story, it shows you the story of how some boy from Coalwood can grow up and be one of the most successful engineers that NASA has ever employed. This story is good for any person who wants a few laughs and i would recommend it to anyone that is looking for a good book to read. Rocket Boys is my all time favorite Boy and i hope it can be yours too.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1777672496021503355">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Jr.<br />Type of book: Non-Fiction<br /> The Number One Rocket<br />Rocket Boys, is a fun and exciting book. A book about a young man and his friends who want to do something with there life's but have know idea what. This book is during a time when all that matted in Coalwood was coal mining and high school football. But when a couple of misfits who have no idea, and little knowledge of what they wanted to be when they grow up, decided one day that they had to have a better future for themselves and that they did not want to be like any ordinary person, that they will go to any means necessary to accomplish there goal. With a little help from some people who believed in them, and with some other people who have to be pushed to believe in them, like Sonny’s father, then they will have accomplished a very successful goal. Rocket Boys is a very powerful kind of story because it shows a journey that will be accomplished, and all the forks in the rode will be diminished, so that they could become something that they wanted to be. With his father against him and his mother supporting him all throughout the journey, Sonny, Roy Lee, Quentin, Sherman, O’Dell, and Tony a.k.a “Rocket Boys”, will have brought a new matter to Coalwood, the matter of which even though you are a Coalwood kid it does not mean you can not succeed in something even though you have believers and disbelievers. That is what the boys of Coalwood, West Virgina were trying to show to the people, that if they can accomplish something that can change the world than anybody can. That is why I recommend you read this book because you wont get bored and you will love every page right when you open the book, from the first page to the very last word.</span>

        <a href="/review/show/118731522?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 26, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3445389-jon" class="user" title="Jon">Jon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96642.Rocket_Boys" title="Paperback 9780385333214" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer118731522">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14313024805820589683">I only have one real complaint with this book. Rocket Boys is ostensibly a work of non-fiction, but the author's note refers to an "author's license" and "certain liberties in the telling of the story." I think this note under-states the extent to which the story has clearly been fictionalized. The too-good-to-be-true coincidences of timing eventually made me realize that the details of this story are not to be taken literally.<br /><br />Otherwise, however, this is a wonderful book. I feel like the world I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14313024805820589683">I only have one real complaint with this book. Rocket Boys is ostensibly a work of non-fiction, but the author's note refers to an "author's license" and "certain liberties in the telling of the story." I think this note under-states the extent to which the story has clearly been fictionalized. The too-good-to-be-true coincidences of timing eventually made me realize that the details of this story are not to be taken literally.<br /><br />Otherwise, however, this is a wonderful book. I feel like the world I grew up in is far, far away from the coal towns of West Virginia, but Rocket Boys really drew me in and helped me understand that life. On the flip side, I felt a great deal of empathy for the thirst for knowledge expressed by the rocket boys.<br /><br />The boys' quest to build rockets that fly higher and higher (or at first, just fly) is fascinating, but perhaps more interesting is Sonny's quest to understand his mother and father. Those two characters come across more strongly than any others in this book (or most others). </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14313024805820589683">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/571879179?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5415704-grace" class="user" title="Grace">Grace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96642.Rocket_Boys" title="Paperback 9780385333214" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">You better read it. I gave it five stars.</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer571879179">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5234668250788978671">Usually, I'm not particularly interested in reading memoirs, but this book is the exception to the rule. <br /><br />Once a upon a time in Earth Science class, when we were learning about space and the planets (I swear we learn it every year, but whatever), our Earth Science teacher decided to show us a film called October Sky. At first, I thought. Oh, another one of those silly science videos they show us every year like Bill Nye the science guy, but worse. I think I'll just take a nap.<br /><br />On the contrary, it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5234668250788978671">Usually, I'm not particularly interested in reading memoirs, but this book is the exception to the rule. <br /><br />Once a upon a time in Earth Science class, when we were learning about space and the planets (I swear we learn it every year, but whatever), our Earth Science teacher decided to show us a film called October Sky. At first, I thought. Oh, another one of those silly science videos they show us every year like Bill Nye the science guy, but worse. I think I'll just take a nap.<br /><br />On the contrary, it was a pretty good movie and I actually enjoyed it. After finishing the film, our teacher mentioned a book that October Sky was the film adaption for, called <em>Rocket Boys</em>. I didn't put too much thought into it at the time, admittedly.<br /><br />A couple months later, after a shameful Battle of the Books loss, I found out the list for the next years Battle of the Books list and surprise (surprise!), <em>Rocket Boys</em> was on it! I grabbed a copy and sat down and began to read it. I figured it would be a slow read since it was a memoir, but as soon as read the first chapter or so, I knew I had to finish the book before I got any sleep.<br /><br />If I had to say thing about the book, it'd be the girl Dorothy Plunk, made me MAD. Geez woman, you know that Homer loves you, but you don't love him, but you still freaking flirt with him?! C'MON NOT COOL. I guess some things don't change at all; things still seem to be the same today, eh?<br /><br />A side note: This is probably the only time I'm going to say this, but I actually thought the film adaption for the book was as good or better than the book. Maybe it was because I watched the movie first; I don't know, but having a visual pretty accurate to the book was nicer than just having to read the words on paper and ink. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5234668250788978671">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText751975355526048677">Rocket Boys<br />Homer H. Hickam Jr.<br />Genre: Autobiography<br />Theme: Follow Your Dreams<br /><br />Sonny (Homer H. Hickam Jr.) is a boy growing up in a cole mining town. His father runs the cole mines and all life in the town of Coalwood revolves around the mining of coal. Sonny is expected by the family to grow up and work in the mines but all we wants to do is design and build rockets. Dr. von Braun's work with Sputnik inspires Sonny and his gang of friends to step outside their normal lifestyles and the town's expectations and follow in his footsteps to build rockets. <br /><br />Quote: Coalwood, West Virginia, where I grew up, was built for the purpose of extracting the millions of tons of rich, bituminous coal that lay beneath it. In 1957, when I was fourteen years old and first began to build my rockets, there were nearly two thousand people living in Coalwood<br />-Homer write from first person and describes his life to us through his own eyes. This style of writing helps the reader feel connected to Sonny and what he accomplishes. <br />-This book would be interesting to anyone over 5th grade both boys and girls who like a longish and realistic read. <br />Movie of Rocket Boys is called: October Sky<br /><br />Fun Fact: R O C K E T B O Y S mix up the letter you get....O C T O B E R S K Y </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer208400449">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12376990335472390394">ROCKET BOYS<br /><br /><br /> Boom! Swish!! Crack!!! Auk XXll leaps into the sky and explodes! You would think that a book about rockets shooting a thousand feet into the air would be exciting. Well, the book Rocket Boys by Homer Hickam, Jr. is probably the furthest thing from exciting. <br /><br /> Sonny Hickam and his friends (O’Dell, Billy, Sherman, Roy Lee) have a special interest for rockets, so they decide to build and fly rockets. They call their club the Rocket Boys. The rockets that they build have problems with fly</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12376990335472390394">ROCKET BOYS<br /><br /><br />	Boom! Swish!! Crack!!! Auk XXll leaps into the sky and explodes! You would think that a book about rockets shooting a thousand feet into the air would be exciting. Well, the book Rocket Boys by Homer Hickam, Jr. is probably the furthest thing from exciting. <br /><br />	Sonny Hickam and his friends (O’Dell, Billy, Sherman, Roy Lee) have a special interest for rockets, so they decide to build and fly rockets. They call their club the Rocket Boys. The rockets that they build have problems with flying askew and exploding, which makes the people of the town angry. Many people in Coalwood want to ban the boys from flying rockets, but they find a special place to shoot rockets so that the town won’t be hurt by exploding rockets. Meanwhile, Sonny falls “in love” with a girl named Dorothy, and tries desperately to win her heart without much success. Eventually, the Rocket Boys enter the science fair, and go all the way to the national competition to win first place! <br /><br />	Although the summary of this book may seem interesting, Homer Hickam takes three hundred and eighty four pages to give dull explanations of only a few events. The story takes place in the 1960’s in Coalwood, West Virginia in a mining town. Since it takes place in a coal mine, mining and coal is very important to the story. I’m not very interested in mining and all those things, so that made the book all the more boring for me. On page 53, it says: “All around me, Coalwood was always busy playing it’s industrial symphony of rumbling coal cars, spouting locomotives, the tromping of the miners going to and from the mine.” This is evidence that the plot of Rocket Boys is very dependent on the setting of a coal mine. <br /><br />	Even though this book was dull, thick, and lacking an exciting plot, the message it gives is a good one, and it is important and applicable to everyday life. Many people in the town of Coalwood discouraged the Rocket Boys from building rockets because it was not convenient for them, but Sonny and his friends kept doing it because it was something they really wanted and were determined enough to work hard. Many people in today’s society listen too much to the opinions and voices of others, and it prevents them from doing great things in their life that they really want to do. The message of Rocket Boys is something everyone should hear. <br /><br />	I would recommend this book to young adults/adults who can get through long, boring plots easily and be entertained by the topic of mining. Although the subject is somewhat mature and occasionally hard to understand, everyone should be taught the lesson that the Rocket Boys learned when they tried their hardest and were finally rewarded for it by winning first place nationally. Remember: Working hard can lead to success, no matter what others say or do to try to stop you. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12376990335472390394">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/792042247?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 17, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/24771958-kayvin-elliott" class="user" title="Kayvin Elliott">Kayvin Elliott</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer792042247">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9120093856829004636">Homer Hickam wrote the story October Sky. The story takes place in Coalwood, West Virginia in 1957, when a group of four boys called the "Rocket Boys" did something no one thought they could ever do. Homer Hickman as a young boy wanted to be a rocket scientist, which is why he put together the small group so they could build a Rocket. They built a rocket called "Sputnik" which failed several times but the four boys never gave up on what they knew was possible. Although no one believed in the boy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9120093856829004636">Homer Hickam wrote the story October Sky. The story takes place in Coalwood, West Virginia in 1957, when a group of four boys called the "Rocket Boys" did something no one thought they could ever do. Homer Hickman as a young boy wanted to be a rocket scientist, which is why he put together the small group so they could build a Rocket. They built a rocket called "Sputnik" which failed several times but the four boys never gave up on what they knew was possible. Although no one believed in the boys they believed in themselves and worked hard at what they wanted to achieve. Homer wanted to prove everyone wrong so he did and the small town boys became successful is exactly what they knew would become successful sooner or later. <br /> On October 5th Homer did something no one ever thought he would do, he built that Rocket of his. Homer always tried to measure up to his brother, and how perfect his brother was but Homer was nothing like his brother no monster athlete or popular he was just Homer. Homer decided to start his own path which was the scientific path. After hearing about a Rocket on the radio Homer had decided he was gonna put together a group that could build a rocket. It took a long long time for Homer and his friends to make the perfect rocket. They almost gave up, but their teacher encouraged them to keep going. She was the only one that believed in the boys. With her help the boys were put into a competition, they faced a lot of obstacles but managed to come out a winner. The boys then got everyone's encouragement and support. At the end of the book you learn that Homer became what he wanted to a scientist and was successful. <br /> The overall theme of this book was to have courage, and to be brave. Without the boys courage to do what they did who knows exactly what they'd be doing today, or without the bravery who knows of they would of gave up. My reaction to this book was "wow" these boys really know what they wanna do in life and are not going to give up. This book helped you realize that if you set your mind to something it is possible. <br /> This book was a long book, but I enjoyed getting to discover the boys talents and what all they went through to get where they were. This book gave you a look at what it is to keep your kind set on that one thing. It really makes you wanna do something that everyone can remember you by. This book is good for Junior High level. It isn't too difficult and is a really fantastic book. This book can honestly teach someone a lot. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer247800461">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17132167517273285436">If I have an absolute favorite book this would have to be it. It is such a wonderful and inspiring story that I recommend it to everyone It is the true story of a group of boys growing up in a tiny coal mining town in rural West Virginia who are so captivated by the sight of the Russian Sputnik satellite orbiting overhead that they decide to build their own rocket. With little information available to them they tackle task by trial and error, often with hilarious results. Inspired by their teach</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17132167517273285436">If I have an absolute favorite book this would have to be it. It is such a wonderful and inspiring story that I recommend it to everyone It is the true story of a group of boys growing up in a tiny coal mining town in rural West Virginia who are so captivated by the sight of the Russian Sputnik satellite orbiting overhead that they decide to build their own rocket. With little information available to them they tackle task by trial and error, often with hilarious results. Inspired by their teacher, and with the backing of their community they teach themselves physics to master rocketry while overcoming numerous obstacles. These are not tiny toy rockets, but rockets capable of soaring miles in the sky. As huge underdogs they even win the national science fair. This is a story of determination, love, friendship, community and hardship. It is so much more than the story of their rockets, it is the story of growing up in a small town in 1950s American. Rocket Boys aka October Skys should be on everyone's must read list.</span>

Among them would be history makers, including the first American woman and the first African American in space. This assem&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText354553280536001332\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;\nOn February 1, 1978, the first group of space shuttle astronauts, twenty-nine men and six women, were introduced to the world. Among them would be history makers, including the first American woman and the first African American in space. This assembly of astronauts would carry NASA through the most tumultuous years of the space shuttle program. Four would die on Challenger.  USAF Colonel Mike Mullane was a member of this astronaut class, and Riding Rockets is his story -- told with a candor never before seen in an astronaut\'s memoir. Mullane strips the heroic veneer from the astronaut corps and paints them as they are -- human. His tales of arrested development among military flyboys working with feminist pioneers and post-doc scientists are sometimes bawdy, often hilarious, and always entertaining.  Mullane vividly portrays every aspect of the astronaut experience -- from telling a female technician which urine-collection condom size is a fit; to walking along a Florida beach in a last, tearful goodbye with a spouse; to a wild, intoxicating, terrifying ride into space; to hearing &amp;quot;Taps&amp;quot; played over a friend\'s grave. Mullane is brutally honest in his criticism of a NASA leadership whose bungling would precipitate the Challenger disaster.  Riding Rockets is a story of life in all its fateful uncertainty, of the impact of a family tragedy on a nine-year-old boy, of the revelatory effect of a machine called Sputnik, and of the life-steering powers of lust, love, and marriage. It is a story of the human experience that will resonate long after the call of &amp;quot;Wheel stop.&amp;quot;\n&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"354553280536001332\" href=\"#\" It is a story that begins with his childhood in Ohio where he learned the importance of family, community, and patriotism. Always a gifted flier, it was during the war that he contemplated the unlimited possibilities of aviation and its frontiers.We see the early days of NASA, where he first served as a backup pilot for astronauts Alan Shepard and Gus Grissom. In 1962 Glenn piloted the Mercury-Atlas 6 Friendship 7 spacecraft on the first manned orbital mission of the United States. In Carrying the Fire, his account of his voyages into space and the years of training that led up to them, Collins reveals the human tensions, the physical realities, and the personal emotions surrounding the early years of the space race. Collins provides readers with an insider\'s view of the space program and conveys the excitement and wonder of his journey to the moon. As skilled at writing as he is at piloting a spacecraft, Collins explains the clash of personalities at NASA and technical aspects of flight with clear, engaging prose, withholding nothing in his candid assessments of fellow astronauts Neil Armstrong, John Glenn, and Buzz Aldrin, and officials within NASA. A fascinating memoir of mankind\'s greatest journey told in familiar, human terms, Carrying the Fire is by turns thrilling, humorous, and thought-provoking, a unique work by a remarkable
